TI DEVELOPMENT OF MICROSTRIP GAS CHAMBERS WITH MULTICHIP TECHNOLOGY
SO NUCLEAR INSTRUMENTS & METHODS IN PHYSICS RESEARCH SECTION A-ACCELERATORS
   SPECTROMETERS DETECTORS AND ASSOCIATED EQUIPMENT
LA English
DT Article; Proceedings Paper
CT 6TH INTERNATIONAL WIRE CHAMBER CONF
CY FEB 17-21, 1992
CL VIENNA, AUSTRIA
SP BUNDESMINIST WISSENSCH & FORSCH, FREMDENVERKEHRSVERBAND WIEN, BUNDESKAMMER GEWERBLICHEN WIRSCH
ID DETECTOR
AB We have developed the microstrip gas chamber (MSGC) by using multi-chip technology which supports high-density assembly of bare LSI chips on a silicon wafer. Our MSGC was operated steadily with approximately 10(3) gain more than one week. An energy resolution of 15% for 5.9 keV X-ray of a Fe-55 source was obtained. With a very thin polyimide substrate of 16 mum thickness, two interesting phenomena were observed; one was a strong dependence of gains on backplane potential, and the other was little time variation of gains. We also found that a guard mask of a thin polyimide layer on the cathode edge reduced incidental electrical discharges between anode and cathode strips.

TI NEGATIVE-PION TRAPPING BY A METASTABLE STATE IN LIQUID-HELIUM
SO PHYSICAL REVIEW A
LA English
DT Article
AB We have found a long-lived metastable state of stopped-pi- in liquid helium by measuring the time spectra of two different delayed products: (i) protons emitted after pi--absorption by He-4 nuclei and (ii) 70-MeV electrons originating from free pi- --> e--nu(e)BAR decay. The lifetime and fraction of delayed pi--absorption obtained by using the emitted protons are 7.26 +/- 0.12 nsec and 1.66 +/- 0.05%, respectively. The free-decay fraction of a pion in liquid helium was obtained to be 0.64 +/- 0.03% from this result, which is consistent with the observed free-pi- decay fraction. These results imply that 2.30 +/- 0.07% of stopped-pi-are trapped in the metastable state which have an overall lifetime of 10.1 +/- 0.2 nsec. The same experimental and analysis were performed for stopped-pi- in liquid neon, where no evidence for trapping was found.

TI PERFORMANCE OF A LARGE SUPERCONDUCTING SPECTROMETER MAGNET - SKS
SO IEEE TRANSACTIONS ON MAGNETICS
LA English
DT Article; Proceedings Paper
CT 12TH INTERNATIONAL CONF ON MAGNET TECHNOLOGY
CY JUN 23-28, 1991
CL ST PETERSBURG, USSR
SP I V KURCHATOV INST ATOM ENERGY, ALL UNION RES & DEV INST CABLE IND, A A BOCHVAR ALL UNION SCI RES INST INORGAN MAT
AB A sector type superconducting spectrometer magnet named SKS for nuclear physics experiments in 1 GeV/c region has been constructed and installed at KEK by Institute for Nuclear Study, University of Tokyo in collaboration with KEK.  It has the maximum central magnetic field of 3 tesla in a magnet gap of 50 cm required by properties of high resolution and large acceptance.  From another requirement to be movable around a target at a cold state, a flexible transfer line is adopted.  The maximum rated current of 500 A is selected to make the heat losses as small as possible.  A small-size refrigerator is used for thermal insulations at 80 and 20 K in combination with a medium-size one at 4 K.

TI THE (PI+,K+) REACTION ON C-12 AND FE-56
SO NUCLEAR PHYSICS A
LA English
DT Article
ID HYPERNUCLEI; POLARIZATION
AB The kaon momentum spectra were measured in the (pi+,K+) reaction on a carbon and an iron target at the KEK 12 GeV proton synchrotron by using of a broad-range medium-resolution spectrometer.  The obtained spectra in the hypernuclear bound region were compared with a DWIA calculation and those in the quasifree region with a Fermi gas model.  It has been shown that these calculations give a good account of the general characteristics of the (pi+,K+) reaction.

TI COINCIDENCE MEASUREMENTS OF (P,N) REACTIONS AT 1.5 GEV/C ON C AND H IN
   THE DELTA-EXCITATION REGION
SO PHYSICAL REVIEW LETTERS
LA English
DT Article
ID NUCLEI; ISOBARS
AB Coincidence measurements of (p,n) reactions at 1.5 GeV/c in the DELTA excitation region have been carried out for the first time.  The location of the DELTA peak in the neutron spectrum is found to be dependent on the coincident particles.  The peak in coincidence with p-pi-+ is shifted to lower momenta compared to the free case, in contrast to the inclusive spectrum and the coincidence with other particles where it is shifted to higher momenta.  The p-pi-+ invariant-mass distribution for C is significantly lower and broader than that for H.  The coincidence data set stringent constraints on theoretical models introduced to interpret the peak shift in inclusive spectra.

TI PROPERTIES OF LARGE-SIZED NB-BASED SUPERCONDUCTING TUNNEL-JUNCTIONS FOR
   X-RAY-DETECTION
SO JAPANESE JOURNAL OF APPLIED PHYSICS PART 1-REGULAR PAPERS SHORT NOTES &
   REVIEW PAPERS
LA English
DT Article
DE NIOBIUM; SUPERCONDUCTING; TUNNEL JUNCTION; X-RAY; QUASI PARTICLE; MEAN
   FREE PATH
AB Niobium-based superconducting tunnel junctions are expected to be applicable to high-resolution X-ray measurements.  Large-sized tunnel junctions with a Nb/Al/AlOx/Nb structure have been fabricated in order to study their performance in X-ray detection.  The niobium layer which was sensitive to X-rays had a large size of 100-mu-m square x 1.2-mu-m thick.  The junction detected 5.9 keV X-rays with an energy resolution of 1 keV.  On the basis of the experimental data, the junction parameters were studied to produce a better energy resolution than that of silicon semiconductor detectors.  The microstructure of the aluminum layer was observed by means of a transmission electron microscope.

TI GENERALIZED PEANO SCANS FOR ARBITRARILY-SIZED ARRAYS
SO IEICE TRANSACTIONS ON COMMUNICATIONS ELECTRONICS INFORMATION AND SYSTEMS
LA English
DT Article
AB The mappings from multidimension to one-dimension, or the inverse mappings, are theoretically discussed as space-filling curves, i.e., Peano curves.  The Peano scan is an application of a Peano curve to the scanning of images, and it is used for analyzing, clustering, or compressing an image, and for limiting the number of the colors used in an image.  The horizontal and vertical sizes of the scanned array, however, must be a power of two.  To avoid such a case, we generalize the Peano scan for scanning an arbitrarily-sized array, whose horizontal and vertical sizes are possible to be different.  First we propose a binary scan which is made of binarily recursive divisions of an image.  As the Peano scan is characterized by the statistical property of Brownian motion, further we describe that binary scan can be also optimized to have such statistical property.

TI CONSTRUCTION OF A LARGE SUPERCONDUCTING SPECTROMETER MAGNET
SO IEEE TRANSACTIONS ON MAGNETICS
LA English
DT Article; Proceedings Paper
CT 1990 CONF ON APPLIED SUPERCONDUCTIVITY
CY SEP 24-28, 1990
CL SNOWMASS, CO
AB A sector type superconducting spectrometer magnet, SKS, for nuclear physics experiments has been constructed by Institute for Nuclear Study, University of Tokyo with collaboration from KEK.  The central magnetic field is 3 tesla with the magnet gap of 50 cm and the stored energy is estimated as 11.2 MJ.  The total weight of the magnet is 280 tons with the iron yoke.  Three dimensional magnetic field calculation and the stress analysis have been performed to design the coil and supporting structures.  The magnet has a flexible helium transfer line to be movable to measure angular distributions at nuclear physics experiments.  To simplify the transfer line, a small-size G-M refrigerator, which is installed on a service port of the helium vessel, is adopted for thermal insulations at 80 K and 20 K in combination with a medium-size refrigerator for cooling the magnet at 4 K.  The heat leak to 4 K is made as small as possible to be able to adopt the refrigeration system.  It is estimated as 3 W at 4 K.  In this point of view, the maximum operation current of 500 A is selected by consideration of the maximum temperature of the coil at quench.  By preliminary cooling test, the magnet has been cooled within 52 hours as expected.  The thermal shields could be cooled for 4 days prior to cooling the magnet.  The magnet has been successfully excited up to the maximum magnetic field of 3.08 tesla without quench.

TI OUTPUT SIGNAL FROM NB-BASED TUNNEL-JUNCTIONS BY IRRADIATION OF 6 KEV
   X-RAYS
SO IEEE TRANSACTIONS ON MAGNETICS
LA English
DT Article; Proceedings Paper
CT 1990 CONF ON APPLIED SUPERCONDUCTIVITY
CY SEP 24-28, 1990
CL SNOWMASS, CO
ID DETECTORS
AB Niobium-based superconducting tunnel junctions are expected to be applicable to high resolution X-ray measurements.  Large-size tunnel junctions with a Nb/Al/AlOx/Nb structure have been fabricated in order to study their performance in X-ray detection.  The junction detected 5.9 keV X-rays with an energy resolution of 1 keV.  Output signal is analyzed by the use of coupled Boltzmann equations.  The method based on these equations clarifies the basic behavior of the quasiparticles and phonons, and the average energy for producing a single electron amounts to 3.2-DELTA.

TI QUASI-FREE C-12(PI+,P) REACTION AND THE PI-N AMPLITUDE IN NUCLEI
SO PHYSICAL REVIEW C
LA English
DT Article
ID SCATTERING
AB Protons knocked out of C-12 by quasifree pion scattering at P-pi approximately 500 MeV/c were measured at forward angles.  The effective nucleon number of the reaction was derived from the energy-integrated cross section divided by the p(pi+,p)pi+ reaction cross section measured simultaneously by using a CH2 target.  The effective nucleon numbers obtained and roughly three times larger than the distorted-wave impulse approximation calculation.  It is shown that the difference is due to the change of the pi-N amplitude in a nucleus because there nucleons are bound and off-mass shell.

TI PRODUCTION AND POLARIZATION OF STRANGE QUARKS FROM NUCLEAR-MATTER -
   POLARIZATION OF LAMBDA HYPERONS AT BACKWARD ANGLES IN THE REACTIONS
   PI-A-]LAMBDA-X AND PI-A-]LAMBDA-KOX AT 4 GEV-C
SO JOURNAL DE PHYSIQUE
LA English
DT Article; Proceedings Paper
CT 7TH INTERNATIONAL CONF ON POLARIZATION PHENOMENA IN NUCLEAR PHYSICS
CY JUL 09-13, 1990
CL PARIS, FRANCE
SP INST NATL PHYS NUCL & PHYS PARTICLES, DIV SCI MATIERE, INT UNION PURE & APPL PHYS
AB A LAMBDA-hyperon is a fascinating nuclear probe at quark level.  By using it, we can study the production of strange quarks from nuclear matter and their polarizations.  Actually, we have measured the polarizations and the differential cross sections of LAMBDA-hyperons produced on C-12 target at backward angles(70-degrees < theta(lab) < 145-degrees), where the production of LAMBDA-hyperon is strongly forbidden in the quasifree interaction of incident pions with nucleons in nucleus, using large-aperture spectrometer.  The polarizations are not reproduced at all by calculation based on the superposition of elementary processes, while both the polarizations and the cross sections are reproduced well in calculation based on the quark-proton models.  As a next step, we have just finished the experiment on Li-6 target, which is also mentioned a little bit.
